materials/editor/prefab_icon.vmat
Prefab
Map File
fixupEntityNames
useTargetNameAsPrefix
loadIfNested
visexclude
displayColor
prefabRuntimeEntity
loadAtRuntime
targetMapPath
Specifies the map file whose contents will be referenced by this prefab.
Target Name
Specifies the name by which the prefab can be referenced by entity i/o. The set of inputs the prefab has is defined by the map relays in the target map.
Fixup entity names
If enabled, any entity target names within the prefab will have a prefix applied to ensure they are unique. This prevents any issues with entities in two different prefabs having name collisions.
Prefix with Target Name
fixupEntityNames == false || targetName == ""
If this is enabled and name fixup is enabled, the prefix used for name fixup will be the prefab target name instead of the unique id. If the target name is empty then the prefab the unique id will still be used as the prefix. Note that if two prefabs use the same target name for their prefix it will be possible to have entities inside the prefabs end up with name collisions.
Load if nested
If enabled the prefab will be loaded when it is the child of another prefab, if disabled, this prefab will not be loaded if it is the child of another prefab.
Not a Vis Contributor
If set, the contents of the prefab will not be included in visibility calculations.
Display Color
A color which will be used to identify the prefab within Hammer, does not have any affect on the compiled map
Create Prefab Runtime Entity
If enabled, there will be a point_prefab entity at runtime representing this prefab as an EntityIO target (requires Relays and a Target Name). Map Relay connections will not be baked, but will instead route through this entity.
Load at runtime
If enabled the prefab will not be baked into the parent map during map compile, but instead will be dynamically loaded in the game. This requires the target map to be compiled separately. Additionally this requires support for dynamic loading of maps by the game, which may not be supported by all games and game systems. Do not use without checking to see if this is fully supported by the game you are working on.

Smart Prop File
vsmart
Specifies the smart prop which this object will instantiate
Whole object tint color
A tint color to apply to the entire smart prop. The evaluation of the smart prop receives this color and may use it directly or may modify it before assigning a tint to the individual parts of the smart prop.
Lock Evaluation
Disable updates from the specified smart prop file.
Constrain To Prefab
If enabled and the smart prop is inside a prefab, the evaluation of the smart prop considers only the contents of the parent prefab, not anything outside the prefab. For example, if enabled, any traces performed by the smart prop will only hit other objects within the parent prefab.
evaluationLocked == true
Input Shapes
Alpha of the fade, where 0 = fully transparent and 255 = fully opaque.
Render Properties
Cull Distance
Maximum distance at which individual parts of the prop will be visible. If 0 the setting on individual parts of the smart prop will be used.
Fade Start Distance
Distance at which each part of the prop starts to fade. Only applies if Cull Distance > 0. Positive values are absolute values, while negative values are relative to the cull distance. For example Cull Distance = 100, Start Fade Distance = -30 means the object will start fading at 70 units away and will disappear when 100 units away.
Select a an entity to specify a location to sample lighting from, instead of using this entity's bounding box center.
Lighting
what type of shadows should be cast from this object.
Baked Lighting Mode
Should baked lighting be generated for this object. If default is selected, the choice is left to individual parts.
Lightprobed
Lightmapped
Lightmap Scale Bias
Increase or decrease the resolution of the lightmap applied to this object.
Scale down by 8
Scale down by 4
Scale down by 2
Default (no scale)
Scale up by 2
Scale up by 4
Scale up by 8
Bake Lighting As If Double-Sided
Bake lighting as if this were double-sided geometry. Useful on geometry with pre-culled backfaces whose neighbors have lighting errors caused by saw-too-many-backfaces sample invalidation.
Collisions
Specifies how collision shapes are to generated.
Build Settings
Not Solid
Use axis-aligned box
Use oriented Box
Use VPhysics
Vis Occluder
If true this geometry is used as an occluder for precomputed visibility
Render To Cubemaps
If true, this geometry renders into baked cube maps
Disable in low quality mode
Do not render when using the lowest quality video settings. This object is a non-essential detail.
Bake To World
If true this geometry will be baked into the world geometry of the map so that the model is not referenced at runtime.
Disable Merging
If true this will not be merged with other geometry during map compile (reduces rendering efficiency).
Render with Dynamic Objects
Render this object with other dynamic objects

CMapDeformerSimple
Y-Axis
Z-Axis
Simple Deformer
bendAxis
bendAngle
bendPoint
bendRadius
Deformation Axis
Specifies the local space axis which the deformer will bend around.
Bend Angle
Specifies the angle of bend to apply in degrees. Range is [ -360, 360 ]. Negative values cause the bend to occur in the opposite direction.
Bend Point
0 to 1 value specifying the location on the local x-axis of the deformer around which the bend will occur. A value of 0 means the bend will occur around the minimum end of the deformer, a value of 1 means the bend will occur around the maximum end of the deformer, a value of 0.5 means the bend will occur at the center of the deformer volume.
Bend Radius
Specifies the radius of the bend. When the value is 0, the radius is automatically calculated to preserve the length of the deformer volume for the specified angle. If an explict radius is specified then the inside edge of the bend will match this radius for all angle values, however this will result the the deformer changing the length of its contents.

CSmartPropElement_FitOnLine
No scaling
Do not allow selected elements to be scaled, the parts may not fit the line exactly
Scale last
Apply scale to the last element in order to fit the line. Only proceed to scale additional elements if the scale range of the last element is not sufficient.
Scale equally
Attempt to apply the same amount of scale to all of the elements placed on the line while still respecting their size constraints.
Maximize scale
Each element will be scaled to is maximum allowable size that will still fit on the line.
SCALE_END_TO_FIT
SCALE_EQUALLY
SCALE_MAXIMIZE
Largest fitting
Pick the largest child element that will fit in the remaining length of the line, repeat this process until the line is full or no child will fit in the remaining length.
Random fitting
Pick a random choice from the child elements that will fit within the remaining length, repeat this process until the line is full or no child will fit in the remaining length.
Place all in order
Place all of the child elements in the order they are specified even if they do not fit the line or do not fill the line. NOTE: end cap settings are ignored in this mode.
LARGEST_FIRST
ALL_IN_ORDER

CSmartPropElement_PickOne
Specifies the method to use to determine which positions this element should be placed at along the path.
( m_PlaceAtPositions == ALL ) || ( m_PlaceAtPositions == START_AND_END ) || ( m_PlaceAtPositions == CONTROL_POINTS )
Specifies the spacing between positions. For example, a value of 1 will place the element at very position, 2 every other position, 3 every third position
Specifies an offset to use when determining the Nth position to place an element at. For example if placing at every third position with an offset of 0, an element will appear at positions 1, 4, 7, and so on. But if an offset of 2 is set instead of 0, then an element will appear at positions 3, 6, and 9 and so on.

Name of the path to use. This path name will show up in the property editor when selecting a placement of this smart prop in Hammer, allowing selection of a path object in the map to use.
Spacing between points on the path
Offset from the start of the path to place the first point.
Offset from path
Offset to apply to the path, specifies a horizontal and vertical offset to apply relative to the up direction.
Path Evaluation Space
Specifies the space in which the provided input path is to be evalauted.<br><br><b>World Space</b>: The input path will be evaluated in world space, such that child elements will be placed directly on the target path regardless of the transform of the smart prop object. <br><b>Object Space</b>: The world space transform of the input path will be ignored and instead the path will be evaluated relative to the transform of the smart prop object. <br><b>Element Space</b>: The world space transform of the input path will be ignored and instead the path will be evaluated relative to the transform of the current element within the smart prop. 
If true, treat the specified up direction as fixed up direction to apply to all elements placed on the path. If false the up direction is just an initial direction.
Compute the spacing distance in the 2d plane defined by the up direction. Most useful when using a fixed up direction, if maintaining a distance in the 2d plane is more important than maintaing distance along the path.
If not using a fixed up direction, provides an initial up direction which will be used to determine the orientation of first element on the path, after that the elements will incrementally update to follow the path and may not match this direction. If Use Fixed Up direction is specified, then all elements will use this direction to deterime their up direction.
A set of points defining a path to use when an external path isn't specified. This will be used in the preview and thumbnail for the smart prop. It will also be used when the smart prop is placed in Hammer before a path is selected.
Place on Path
An element which places an instance of its child elements at a specified interval along a path.

Minimum slope on which the target will be placed. Slope is a [ 0, 180 ] value of the surface normal rotation from up such that 0 is a horizontal surface (floor), 90 is a vertical surface (wall), 180 is horizontal upside down surface (ceiling).
